                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-118305401687">

                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-118305401687" style="max-width:305px;">

                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="author-name Font-C-2-140 D-b">
                            <a class="attribution-name Font-C-2-140 Fw-b Whs-n" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:c918bbd2-5444-3fd6-bc35-0ec7e05fe53f;t9:17;elm:itm;elmt:link;itc:0" href="https://twitter.com/amycapetta" style="color:#000;" target="_blank">
                             Amy Capetta
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             May 6, 2015
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-118305401687" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="Broccoli, Watercress May Hold Potent Cancer-Fighting Powers  Unlocked By Chewing" height="540" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/27c5da4b7d5ac8c048ddd0c15701355446b61ca3.jpg" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           <i>
                            Chop that broccoliwith your teeth!
                           </i>
                          </b>
                          <i>
                           (Photo: Getty Images)
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Were well aware that vegetables contain multiple nutrients and supply the body with an abundance of health benefits. And now
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:c918bbd2-5444-3fd6-bc35-0ec7e05fe53f;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.sdstate.edu/news/articles/plant-derived-compound-may-reduce-cancer-recurrence.cfm" target="_blank">
                           a team of researchers from South Dakota State University
                          </a>
                          has found that a compound and an enzyme found in cruciferous vegetables  such as broccoli, watercress, cabbage and cauliflower  may help prevent recurrence and spread of some cancers.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:c918bbd2-5444-3fd6-bc35-0ec7e05fe53f;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.sdstate.edu/resources/directory/directory-detail.cfm?view=detail&amp;ci=2539" target="_blank">
                           Moul Dey
                          </a>
                          , lead study author and associate professor in the Health and Nutritional Sciences Department at the university, explains that even after a cancerous tumor has been eliminated through chemotherapy and/or radiation, the cancer stem cells continue to live on in the body since they tend to be resistant to conventional therapies. While these stem cells only make up about five percent of the tumor, they can migrate through the blood vessels and metastasize.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          These tiny cells are very difficult to detect in a tumor, she says. Its like finding a needle in a haystack.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Related:
                           <i>
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:c918bbd2-5444-3fd6-bc35-0ec7e05fe53f;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/health/why-your-brain-is-obsessed-with-food-at-night-118298758727.html" target="_blank">
                             Why Your Brain Is Obsessed With Food at Night
                            </a>
                           </i>
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          In a Petri dish, Dey and her colleagues treated human cervical cancer stem cells with PEITC  a compound that stands for phenethyl isothiocyanate, which is naturally produced from the crunchy cruciferous veggies during the chewing process. Within 24 hours, nearly 75 percent of the stem cells died.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          In this trial, the researchers used a 20-micromolar concentration of the compound. However, lower concentrations of PEITC were used in subsequent experiments with mice  between five to 15 micromolars  and also were found to produce effective results. Consuming just a few ounces will give you the concentrations we worked with, Dey tells Yahoo Health. We found it worked in mice, but not every study that works in mice will work in humans. But its vegetables  it always has some benefits anyway. You cannot go wrong with having vegetables with every meal.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The study notes that these concentrations were particularly found in land cress and watercress. Other members of the cruciferous crew include Brussels sprouts, kale, radishes, turnips, arugula, bok choy and rutabaga.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Related:
                           <i>
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:c918bbd2-5444-3fd6-bc35-0ec7e05fe53f;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/health/20-filling-foods-that-help-you-lose-weight-104111362483.html" target="_blank">
                             20 Filling Foods That Help You Lose Weight
                            </a>
                           </i>
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          As for those who prefer to drink their veggies in a smoothie  as opposed to chewing them  Dey says its just fine. It just needs some physical force to break the cells, she explains. And those two things that are within the cells of the vegetables simply need to come in contact with each other.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          This is not the first time broccoli and its relatives have been known to possess cancer-fighting properties. The website for the
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:c918bbd2-5444-3fd6-bc35-0ec7e05fe53f;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.cancer.org/treatment/treatmentsandsideeffects/complementaryandalternativemedicine/dietandnutrition/broccoli" target="_blank">
                           American Cancer Society
                          </a>
                          cites previous studies on this topic. For example, a population-based study found that those who ate diets high in lutein, a vitamin Alike chemical obtained from vegetables such as broccoli, spinach, and lettuce, had fewer cases of colon cancer.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Related:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:c918bbd2-5444-3fd6-bc35-0ec7e05fe53f;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/health/how-to-make-smarter-midnight-snack-choices-110662496133.html" target="_blank">
                            <i>
                             How To Make Smarter Midnight Snack Choices
                            </i>
                           </a>
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Another study suggested that those who ate cruciferous vegetables seemed to have a lower risk for bladder cancer. They also refer to another study, which discovered a substance in broccoli (indole-3-carbinol, or I3C) that appeared to alter estrogen levels, as well as raise levels of protective enzymes in the body. And as a result, various trials of cancer cells growing in laboratory dishes or flasks have shown this substance may slow or stop the growth of breast, prostate and other cancer cells.
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:999999px;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                          Bottom line: Eat your broccoli!
                         </p>
                         <p>

                      <div class="item-text">
                       <div class="item-tag Tt-u Font-C-1-115 Fw-b" style="margin-left:175px;">
                        <a class="tag" data-action-outcome="navigate" data-ylk="g:1487ee54-a9a3-38dc-b369-2466cc38c526;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:also;ad:0;cpos:2;itc:0;t9:48;elm:itm;elmt:cat" href="/health/tagged/fitness" style="color:#999;">

                        </a>
                       </div>
                       <a data-action-outcome="open" data-routable-url="/health/1/stomach-vacuuming-easiest-way-to-flat-abs-or-too-124015211072.html" data-ylk="g:1487ee54-a9a3-38dc-b369-2466cc38c526;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:also;ad:0;cpos:2;itc:0;t8:tileview;t9:21;elm:img;elmt:ct;" href="/health/stomach-vacuuming-easiest-way-to-flat-abs-or-too-124015211072.html" style="color:#000;">
                        <span class="item-title Font-A-3-120 D-b" style="word-wrap:break-word;margin-left:175px;">
                         Stomach Vacuuming: Easiest Way to Flat Abs or Too Good to Be True?
                        </span>

But does it work?","body":"\u003Cp\u003EThere&#x2019;s a new abdominal technique in town, and it has an unusual name. But stomach vacuuming isn&#x2019;t as weird as it sounds.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s a breathing exercise that&#x2019;s supposed to activate and strengthen your transverse abdominis (i.e. your deepest ab muscle) by contracting it. Stomach vacuuming experts swear it&#x2019;ll help tighten your abs while stabilizing your spine and improving your posture.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?t=50&amp;v=N9msEniBkbU\"\u003Eone YouTube video\u003C\u002Fa\u003E on the technique, you can do a stomach vacuum while standing, sitting, kneeling, or lying on your back. All you need to do is breathe through your nose for up to five seconds, exhale through your mouth, draw your belly button into your spine, and hold it for several seconds before starting again.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAnd then flat abs are yours! &#x2026;Or not, since several fitness experts aren&#x2019;t exactly buying it.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I couldn&#x2019;t list one fitness expert who uses this exercise &#x2014; I sure as heck don&#x2019;t,&#x201D; personal trainer \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnicktumminello.com\"\u003ENick Tumminello\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, owner of Performance University International, and author of Strength Training for Fat Loss, tells Yahoo Health.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EFitness expert and athletic trainer \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftonygentilcore.com\u002F\"\u003ETony Gentilcore\u003C\u002Fa\u003E seconds that, telling Yahoo Health, &#x201C;I&#x2019;m someone who doesn&#x2019;t agree with the stomach vacuuming maneuver.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBut&#x2026;why not? \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to Tumminello, repeatedly doing stomach vacuuming will just make you better at stomach vacuuming. While you have to use your stomach muscles to do the technique, you&#x2019;re not adding any additional weight to it that will take your abs to the next level.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;You&#x2019;re not going to exceed what your body is already capable of,&#x201D; says Tumminello. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s like doing strength training by opening your mail.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EGentilcore says abdominal strength (and, by extension, helping people with lower back pain) is more about synchronization and getting several muscles to fire at one time. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s not about isolating one teeny-tiny muscle with vague, often cumbersome drills,&#x201D; he says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EPersonal trainer Doug Sklar, owner of New York City&#x2019;s \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fphilanthrofit.com\u002F\"\u003EPhilanthroFIT\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, tells Yahoo Health that doing stomach vacuuming won&#x2019;t hurt you &#x2014; it just won&#x2019;t &#x201C;significantly enhance your progress.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAs for the posture claims, Tumminello calls them &#x201C;total bulls&#x2014;.&#x201D; &#x201C;Posture is habitual,&#x201D; he says. &#x201C;Saying something will improve your posture by squeezing this one muscle for a few seconds&#x2026;well, it can, temporarily.&#x201D; After you&#x2019;ve finished vacuuming, he says, you just revert back to your normal posture. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETumminello doesn&#x2019;t agree with the lower pack pain-reliever claims, either. He cites \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov\u002Fpubmed\u002F9493770\"\u003Eresearch\u003C\u002Fa\u003E conducted in the &#x2018;90s by physiotherapist Paul Hodges that found the transverse abdominis, which is part of your core, has a delayed activation in people who suffer from lower back pain. Many people misinterpreted that as the reason why we have lower back pain but &#x201C;it&#x2019;s a symptom of back pain, not the cause of it,&#x201D; says Tumminello.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EStill want flat abs?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#xA0;Gentilcore says it&#x2019;s going to take more than a few breathing exercises.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHe recommends palloff presses (which involve pulling a cable attached to a weight machine toward your sternum) and farmer carries (walking while carrying a weight in each hand), both of which train your entire core and help improve stability and strength in that area. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESklar points out that there is no quick fix or secret exercise that, by itself, will flatten your abs, since &#x201C;all the stomach vacuuming in the world can&#x2019;t make up for otherwise inconsistent exercise and nutrition habits.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMoral of the story: If an exercise sounds too good to be true, it probably 40\u002F097fd60b9b6c862215909a9c50c0a5260010c767.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":540,"height":434,"size_type":"original","formats":{}}],"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FDnJrMY4-snLcV5q61ywNJ0j6_U8","source_url":"http:\u002F\u002F41.media.tumblr.com\u002F8b53ddf61b7062b1e2947b19ce24351f\u002Ftumblr_inline_nrg5r42xop1t4rmqt_540.jpg"}],"highlight_color":"#000000","data_version":"1","title":"Pentagon Announces Plan Aimed at Lifting Transgender Ban in Military","summary":"Defense Secretary Ash Carter says the Pentagons current regulations banning transgender individuals from serving in the military are outdated, and anyone willing to serve the country should be able to do so.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F097fd60b9b6c862215909a9c50c0a5260010c767.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"434\" alt=\"Pentagon Announces Plan Aimed at Lifting Transgender Ban in Military\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EOver the next six months, a working group in at the Pentagon will be studying the impact of lifting the military&#x2019;s transgender ban.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDefense Secretary Ash Carter says the Pentagon&#x2019;s current regulations banning transgender individuals from serving in the military are outdated, and anyone willing to serve the country should be able to do so.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECarter is creating a working group to do a six-month study on the impact of lifting the ban. Carter says the group will begin with the presumption that transgender people should be able to serve openly.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe plan, which was first reported by The Associated Press, gives the services time to work through questions about health care, housing, physical standards, uniforms and costs associated with the change.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDuring that time, transgender individuals would still be unable to join the military, but decisions to force out those already serving would be referred to the Pentagon&#x2019;s acting undersecretary for personnel.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWith the six-month study, military chiefs wanted time to methodically work through the legal, medical and administrative issues and develop training to ease any transition, and senior leaders believed six months would be sufficient.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe officials said Defense Secretary Ash Carter has asked his personnel undersecretary, Brad Carson, to set up a working group of senior military and civilian leaders to take an objective look at the issue. One senior official said that while the goal is to lift the ban, Carter wants the working group to look at the practical effects, including the costs, and determine whether it would affect readiness or create any insurmountable problems that could derail the plan. The group would also develop uniform guidelines.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fsenior-airman-logan-ireland-is-one-of-over-15-000-120775992272.html\"\u003ETransgender Troops - At War, In Love, and Fighting to Serve Openly\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDuring the six months, transgender individuals would still not be able to join the military, but any decisions to force out those already serving would be referred to the Pentagon&#x2019;s acting undersecretary for personnel, the officials said. One senior official said the goal was to avoid forcing any transgender service members to leave during that time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESeveral officials familiar with the planning spoke on condition of anonymity because they were not authorized to talk about the issue publicly before the final details have been worked out.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn a statement to The Associated Press, Carter said, &#x201C;we must ensure that everyone who&#x2019;s able and willing to serve has the full and equal opportunity to do so. And we must treat all of our people with the dignity and respect they deserve. Going forward the Department of Defense must and will continue to improve how we do both.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESome of the key concerns involved in the repeal of the ban include whether the military would conduct or pay for the medical costs, surgeries and other treatment associated with any gender transition, as well as which physical training or testing standards transgender individuals would be required to meet during different stages of their transition.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOfficials said the military also wants time to tackle questions about where transgender troops would be housed, what uniforms they would wear, what berthing they would have on ships, which bathrooms they would use and whether their presence would affect the ability of small units to work well together. The military has dealt with many similar questions as it integrated the ranks by race, gender and sexual orientation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETransgender people &#x2014; those who identify with a different gender than they were born with and sometimes take hormone treatments or have surgery to develop the physical characteristics of their preferred gender &#x2014; are banned from military service. But studies and other surveys have estimated that as many as 15,000 transgender people serve in the active duty military and the reserves, often in secret but in many cases with the knowledge of their unit commander or peers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Obviously this isn&#x2019;t finished, but Secretary Carter&#x2019;s clear statement of intent means that transgender service members should and will be treated with the same dignity as other service members,&#x201D; said Allyson Robinson, Army veteran and policy director for an association of lesbian, gay, bisexual and transgender military personnel called Service members, Partners, and Allies for Respect and Tolerance for All, or SPARTA.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe move follows several weeks of high level meetings in the Pentagon among top ranking military chiefs, secretaries and Defense Department leaders, including one on Monday involving Carter and the chiefs of the various services.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMilitary leaders have pointed to the gradual - and ultimately successful - transition after the ban on gays serving openly in the military was lifted in 2011. Although legislation repealing that ban passed Congress in late 2010, the military services spent months conducting training and reviews before the decision actually took effect the following September.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fsee-a-transgender-mans-joy-as-he-hones-his-new-121760390117.html\"\u003ESee a Transgender Man&#x2019;s Joy as He Hones His New Body &#x2014; and Meet the Gym That Got Him There&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe latest Pentagon move comes just weeks after the Supreme Court upheld the right of same-sex couples to marry.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOfficials familiar with the Pentagon meetings said the chiefs of the Army, Navy, Marine Corps and Air Force did not express opposition to lifting the ban. Instead, they said the military leaders asked for time to figure out health care, housing and other questions and also to provide information and training to the troops to insure a smooth transition.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlthough guidelines require that transgender individuals be dismissed from the military, the services in recent months have required more senior leaders to make the final decisions on those cases, effectively slowing the dismissal process.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe transgender issue came to the fore as the military struggled with how to deal with convicted national security leaker Chelsea Manning&#x2019;s request for hormone therapy and other treatment while she&#x2019;s in prison. Manning, arrested as Bradley Manning, is the first transgender military prisoner to request such treatment, and the Army approved the hormone therapy, under pressure from a lawsuit.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EManning, is serving a 35-year sentence. The former intelligence analyst was convicted in August 2013 of espionage and other offenses for sending more than 700,000 classified documents to WikiLeaks while working in Iraq.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca or even days later  without additional exposure to the substance that caused the allergic reaction.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fba024d5cd9f04549fb8321a2172aea4664756a8e.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"367\" alt=\"Kids with Severe Allergies Susceptible to &#x2018;Rebound&#x2019; Reactions, Study Finds\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThese delayed reactions tend to occur when the initial symptoms of an allergic reaction go away, but then return hours or even days later &#x2014; without additional exposure to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F36041-common-food-allergies.html\"\u003Esubstance that caused the allergic reaction.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s fairly common for children who have a severe allergic reaction known as anaphylaxis to be in danger of having a second, delayed allergic reaction within hours of the first one, a new study suggests.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EResearchers in Canada found that about 15 percent of children who came to the emergency room for anaphylaxis had a second \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F48636-this-girl-nearly-died-from-orange-allergy.html\"\u003Eserious allergic reaction hours\u003C\u002Fa\u003E after the initial reaction.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe study also found that about 75 percent of these second anaphylactic reactions, known as biphasic reactions, occurred within 6 hours of their first anaphylaxis symptoms, and in most cases, the children were still at the ER because of their first reaction. The children&#x2019;s symptoms included difficulty breathing, low blood pressure, hives or swelling, nausea and dizziness.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The study found that delayed reactions were more likely to happen if the initial allergic reaction in children was severe, and if it was not treated with epinephrine,&#x201D; said Dr. Waleed Alqurashi, the study&#x2019;s lead author and an emergency physician at Children&#x2019;s Hospital of Eastern Ontario in Ottawa, Canada.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F35479-nine-weirdest-allergies-110215.html\"\u003E8\u003Ci\u003E Strange Signs You&#x2019;re Having an Allergic Reaction\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThese delayed reactions tend to occur when the initial symptoms of an allergic reaction go away, but then return hours or even days later &#x2014; without additional exposure to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F36041-common-food-allergies.html\"\u003Esubstance that caused the allergic reaction\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOne possible reason children may develop these delayed allergic reactions is that they seem to experience an inflammatory response that lasts longer than it does in adults, Alqurashi said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn children, common triggers of these serious allergic reactions might include insect stings, medications, and foods like nuts, seafood, milk and eggs, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAn anaphylactic reaction is a medical emergency requiring immediate treatment with a shot of the hormone epinephrine (adrenaline). Many kids who are at risk of having these serious allergic reactions are advised to carry \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F42321-know-how-to-use-epipen.html\"\u003Ean EpiPen\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a prescription medication that can be self-administered or given by a parent or school nurse, to control symptoms that can come on rapidly and worsen quickly and, in some cases, be fatal. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EDelayed treatment\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe occurrence of anaphylactic reactions in children seems to be on the rise, according to the researchers. But there&#x2019;s limited information about how frequently children go on to have a second severe allergic reaction, or about which children might be more vulnerable to having them.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the study, published online June 22 in the journal Annals of Allergy, Asthma and Immunology, the researchers analyzed the medical records of about 500 children who were treated at the emergency rooms of two large Canadian children&#x2019;s hospitals over a one-year period.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe findings suggested that children who may be at increased risk for delayed allergic reactions are those who were given medications for asthma at the hospital, had signs of anaphylactic shock when they arrived at the emergency room and needed multiple treatments with epinephrine for their initial anaphylactic reaction, Alqurashi said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn addition, the results showed that anaphylaxis tended to be more severe in children when epinephrine administration was delayed.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Epinephrine is the single \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F41181-obama-signs-epipen-law.html\"\u003Emost important treatment for anaphylaxis\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,&#x201D; Alqurashi said. He explained that, when the drug is given promptly after the start of an allergic reaction, it controls and limits the immune system&#x2019;s response to a known allergy trigger. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The key message for parents, caregivers and first responders is to administer epinephrine at the first sign of a severe allergic reaction to prevent anaphylaxis from worsening,&#x201D; Alqurashi said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAfter that, people should get to the emergency room, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from Allergies\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca Injuries: One Womans StoryUnderscores Importance of Simple Safety Tips","summary":"As was her regular routine, 57-year-old sales exec Yvonne Myers stepped on the treadmill at her local gym for a run. That's when disaster struck. My nose and face were cut to pieces and my arms were throbbing from burns.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F7bb416f3afaefea452e070c44263cef1985b0d6b.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" alt=\"Treadmill Injuries: One Woman&#x2019;s Story&#xA0;Underscores Importance of Simple Safety Tips\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x201C;My nose and face were cut to pieces and my arms were throbbing from burns.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs was her regular routine, 57-year-old sales exec Yvonne Myers stepped on the treadmill at her local gym for a run. She did not expect, however, for the machine to throw her to the ground the moment she stepped on.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe treadmill&#x2019;s previous user had not turned the machine off, and the belt was spinning at such a fast clip that it looked motionless. When Myers hit the surface, she tried to get up, but was tossed from the exercise machine instead.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;My nose and face were cut to pieces and my arms were throbbing from burns,&#x201D; the South Manchester, UK mother-of-four told \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.dailymail.co.uk\u002Ffemail\u002Farticle-3158486\u002FMaimed-TREADMILL-Mother-four-s-horror-one-thousands-badly-injured-running-machine.html\"\u003EThe Daily Mail\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. &#x201C;I also had a gash on my forehead. I looked as though I&#x2019;d been in a fight.&quot;Even regular gym-goers like Myers, who was an avid treadmill user, are not immune to the dangers of this piece of exercise equipment.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis also isn&#x2019;t the first time treadmill accidents have made news in recent months.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESurveyMonkey CEO Dave Goldberg, husband of Facebook COO Sheryl Sandberg, died this year in a tragic treadmill accident. On May 1, he fell off a machine while on vacation in Mexico, potentially \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.people.com\u002Farticle\u002Fsheryl-sandberg-husband-died-heart-related-causes-dave-goldberg\"\u003Edue to heart complications\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and sustained a head injury, according to a report in \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2015\u002F05\u002F05\u002Ftechnology\u002Fdave-goldberg-cause-of-death.html?smid=nytnow-share&amp;smprod=nytnow&amp;_r=0\"\u003EThe New York Times\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWe don&#x2019;t often think of danger when we head to the gym, but stepping on a treadmill always poses risks. In 2014, around 24,400 injuries occurred as the direct result of treadmill use &#x2014; almost 40 percent of the 62,600 injuries from exercise equipment, making these machines the most dangerous you&#x2019;ll find in your gym.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EDeaths\u003C\u002Fi\u003E from treadmill use, on the other hand, are much rarer, according to U.S. Consumer Product Safety Commission data. Only 30 fatalities from treadmills were reported between 2003 and 2012, for an average of just three per yearHere are some checks to make before you start exercising, or while you&#x2019;re in the middle of a workout, from Michael Jonesco, MD, a sports medicine physician at The Ohio State University Wexner Medical Center:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EEnter with a clean bill of health.\u003C\u002Fb\u003EYour top priority before you hit the gym is to make sure you know your health status. &#x201C;A lot of times we&#x2019;ll see, if you&#x2019;re running, why did he collapse?&#x201D;Jonesco tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;The most common cause of falling is a vascular event, like a heart attack. I don&#x2019;t know this case, but before you start a workout, always make sure you have a clean bill of health. Continue to be screened for coronary issues, even if you feel healthy &#x2013; especially if you have risk factors like age, being male, or a high-stress job.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBeware of strange symptoms.\u003C\u002Fb\u003EIf you&#x2019;re on the treadmill and you feel any chest pain, any shortness of breath beyond what you&#x2019;re used to in a given workout, or any lightheadedness, you need to step off. &#x201C;Lightheadedness is one most people don&#x2019;t think of,&#x201D;says Jonesco. &#x201C;But it can show you&#x2019;re not getting enough blood supply to the brain, and be a preceding factor for passing out.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EDon\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003Et add distractions (until you\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003Ere comfortable).\u003C\u002Fb\u003EBesides coronary issues, other reasons for treadmill falls can usually be pinned to distraction. &#x201C;Usually you have a comfort zone if you&#x2019;re on a machine you&#x2019;re used to, but if you&#x2019;re on vacation or using an unfamiliar machine, you want to take time to get used to it,&#x201D;Jonesco says. Start your workout at a slower pace, be aware of the width of the band, and ditch the headphones or TV until you find your rhythm.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F7-treadmill-mistakes-you-might-be-making-91318038937.html?soc_src=mail&amp;soc_trk=ma\"\u003ETreadmill Mistakes You May Be Making\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EUse the safety tabs. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EYou know the attachments on the treadmill, that are meant to immediately stop the machine if you step out of line? They might be annoying, but use &#x2018;em, says Jonesco. &#x201C;A lot of people overlook the safety tabs because they&#x2019;re clunky, but they&#x2019;re there for a reason.&#x201D;Those attachments could prevent a fall, and are especially important if your treadmill is close to the wall in an unfamiliar area. &#x201C;I like to move the machine away from the wall if at all possible,&#x201D;Jonesco says. &#x201C;If you fall and it doesn&#x2019;t turn off, you can get pushed up against the wall, the band will keep moving and can give you some pretty bad abrasions.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EKeep help nearby.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003EAccording to the report, Goldberg wasn&#x2019;t found by his brother until 7 p.m., although he left for the gym at 4 p.m. Although the gym seems pretty safe, still tell someone you&#x2019;re going &#x2014; or preferably, take them along. &#x201C;Have a workout buddy, or at least familiarize yourself with the people around you at the gym or the staff if something were to happen,&#x201D;says Jonesco. &#x201C;Keep your cell phone nearby you in case of an emergency.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F7-ways-to-make-your-treadmill-runs-more-effective-107228499668.html?soc_src=mail&amp;soc_trk=ma\"\u003E7 Ways To Make Your Treadmill Run More Effective&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENevertheless, exercise is essential. Just, like anything, don&#x2019;t take safety as a given. Always be smart about using equipment, says Jonesco. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s very sad, and could have been a freak thing,&#x201D;he explains. &#x201C;The benefits of exercise far, far exceed the risks.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! Watercress May Hold Potent Cancer-Fighting Powers  Unlocked By Chewing","summary":"A team of researchers has found that a compound found in cruciferous vegetables may help prevent recurrence and spread of some cancers.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F27c5da4b7d5ac8c048ddd0c15701355446b61ca3.jpg\" alt=\"Broccoli, Watercress May Hold Potent Cancer-Fighting Powers &#x2014; Unlocked By Chewing\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EChop that broccoli&#x2026;with your teeth!\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ci\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWe&#x2019;re well aware that vegetables contain multiple nutrients and supply the body with an abundance of health benefits. And now \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.sdstate.edu\u002Fnews\u002Farticles\u002Fplant-derived-compound-may-reduce-cancer-recurrence.cfm\"\u003Ea team of researchers from South Dakota State University\u003C\u002Fa\u003E has found that a compound and an enzyme found in cruciferous vegetables &#x2014; such as broccoli, watercress, cabbage and cauliflower &#x2014; may help prevent recurrence and spread of some cancers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.sdstate.edu\u002Fresources\u002Fdirectory\u002Fdirectory-detail.cfm?view=detail&amp;ci=2539\"\u003EMoul Dey\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, lead study author and associate professor in the Health and Nutritional Sciences Department at the university, explains that even after a cancerous tumor has been eliminated through chemotherapy and\u002For radiation, the cancer stem cells continue to live on in the body since they tend to be resistant to conventional therapies. While these stem cells &#x201C;only&#x201D; make up about five percent of the tumor, they can migrate through the blood vessels and metastasize. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;These tiny cells are very difficult to detect in a tumor,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s like finding a needle in a haystack.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fwhy-your-brain-is-obsessed-with-food-at-night-118298758727.html\"\u003EWhy Your Brain Is Obsessed With Food at Night&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn a Petri dish, Dey and her colleagues treated human cervical cancer stem cells with PEITC &#xA0;&#x2014; a compound that stands for phenethyl isothiocyanate, which is naturally produced from the crunchy cruciferous veggies during the chewing process. Within 24 hours, nearly 75 percent of the stem cells died. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn this trial, the researchers used a 20-micromolar concentration of the compound. However, lower concentrations of PEITC were used in subsequent experiments with mice &#x2014; between five to 15 micromolars &#x2014; and also were found to produce effective results. &#x201C;Consuming just a few ounces will give you the concentrations we worked with,&#x201D; Dey tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;We found it worked in mice, but not every study that works in mice will work in humans. But it&#x2019;s vegetables &#x2014; it always has some benefits anyway. You cannot go wrong with having vegetables with every meal.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe study notes that these concentrations were particularly found in land cress and watercress. Other members of the cruciferous crew include Brussels sprouts, kale, radishes, turnips, arugula, bok choy and rutabaga. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ci\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F20-filling-foods-that-help-you-lose-weight-104111362483.html\"\u003E20 Filling Foods That Help You Lose Weight\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs for those who prefer to drink their veggies in a smoothie &#x2014; as opposed to chewing them &#x2014; Dey says it&#x2019;s just fine. &#x201C;It just needs some physical force to break the cells,&#x201D; she explains. &#x201C;And those two things that are within the cells of the vegetables simply need to come in contact with each other.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis is not the first time broccoli and its relatives have been known to possess cancer-fighting properties. The website for the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cancer.org\u002Ftreatment\u002Ftreatmentsandsideeffects\u002Fcomplementaryandalternativemedicine\u002Fdietandnutrition\u002Fbroccoli\"\u003EAmerican Cancer Society\u003C\u002Fa\u003E cites previous studies on this topic. For example, a population-based study found that those who ate diets high in lutein, a vitamin A&#x2013;like chemical obtained from vegetables such as broccoli, spinach, and lettuce, had fewer cases of colon cancer.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fhow-to-make-smarter-midnight-snack-choices-110662496133.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EHow To Make Smarter Midnight Snack Choices\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnother study suggested that those who ate cruciferous vegetables seemed to have a lower risk for bladder cancer. They also refer to another study, which discovered a substance in broccoli (indole-3-carbinol, or I3C) that appeared to alter estrogen levels, as well as raise levels of protective enzymes in the body. And as a result, various trials of cancer cells growing in laboratory dishes or flasks have shown this substance may slow or stop the growth of breast, prostate and other cancer cells. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBottom line: Eat your broccoli!&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch!
